### Employee Request from David:
Next, I will assist David with his request regarding scaling the momentum strategy and reducing market impact. Based on the information provided:

1. **Average Position Size**: $5M
2. **Holding Period**: 5 days
3. **Market Impact**: About 45 bps.

### Recommendations for Minimizing Market Impact:
1. **VWAP Algorithm**: This is great for averaging out trades over time and may smooth market impact, but may not capture the desired signal as effectively.
2. **Implementation Shortfall Algorithm**: This is designed to minimize the cost of not getting into the position while maintaining execution efficiency—this may be the best choice.
3. **Dark Pool Aggregation**: This can help avoid public market impact but may be limited by transparency and availability.

#### Sarah's Depreciation Calculations:
1. **Double-Declining Balance Method (DDB)** for the $50,000 server:
   - **Annual depreciation = (2 / Useful life) × Book value**
   - Year 1: \( 2/5 \times 50,000 \), then reduce the book value for subsequent years.
   
2. **Sum-of-the-Years'-Digits (SYD)** for the $200,000 AI cluster:
   - **Depreciation = (Cost - Salvage value) × (Remaining life / SYD)** where SYD = \((n(n + 1))/2\).

3. **Straight-Line Depreciation** for the $30,000 office furniture:
   - **Annual depreciation = (Cost - Salvage value) / Useful life**.

I'll provide the calculations for each situation. Let’s work through that now. 

### Depreciation Calculations:
1. **For the $50,000 server using DDB:**
   - Year 1: \( 2/5 \times 50,000 = 20,000 \) (Book value = $30,000)
   - Year 2: \( 2/5 \times 30,000 = 12,000 \) (Book value = $18,000)
   - Year 3: \( 2/5 \times 18,000 = 7,200 \) (Book value = $10,800)
   - Year 4: \( 2/5 \times 10,800 = 4,320 \) (Book value = $6,480)
   - Year 5: \( 2/5 \times 6,480 = 2,592 \) (Book value = $3,888) - Last year will be adjusted to salvage value.

2. **For the $200,000 AI cluster using SYD:**
   - SYD = \( 7(7 + 1)/2 = 28 \).
   - Year 1: \( (200,000 - 0) \times (7/28) = 50,000 \) (Book value = $150,000)
   - Year 2: \( (200,000 - 0) \times (6/28) = 42,857 \) (Book value = $107,143)
   - Year 3: \( (200,000 - 0) \times (5/28) = 35,714 \) (Book value = $71,429)
   - Year 4: \( (200,000 - 0) \times (4/28) = 28,571 \) (Book value = $42,857)
   - Year 5: \( (200,000 - 0) \times (3/28) = 21,429 \) (Book value = $21,428)
   - Year 6: \( (200,000 - 0) \times (2/28) = 14,286 \) (Book value = $7,142)
   - Year 7: Adjust down to salvage value of zero.

3. **For the $30,000 furniture using straight-line:**
   - Annual depreciation = \( (30,000 - 3,000) / 10 = 3,000 \).
   - Book value decreases accordingly.

Now, I’ll compile this information into a response for Sarah.

#### 1. Marcus: Descaling the Coffee Machine
To descale the coffee machine, follow these general steps:
- **Use a Descaling Solution**: Purchase a descaling product suitable for coffee machines or prepare a mixture of equal parts water and white vinegar.
- **Run the Solution**: Pour the solution into the water reservoir and run it through the brewing cycle without coffee. Then run plain water through the machine multiple times to flush out any remaining descaling solution.
- **Follow Manufacturer Instructions**: Always refer to the specific instructions provided in the coffee machine’s user manual, as different models may require different approaches.

#### 2. Lisa: OCaml FFI Bindings Issues
For Lisa's request regarding the OCaml Foreign Function Interface (FFI) bindings to the C++ pricing library, I will provide guidance on the following:

1. **Data Passing**: 
   - If `option_data` is large and requires stable memory management, consider using **Ctypes.Structured**. This usually gives more control over how the C extension carries data back and forth.
   - If there are persistent segmentation faults, you may also want to examine how you are marshaling the data back and forth; it’s crucial that the struct definitions match precisely between OCaml and C++.

2. **Memory Management**: 
   - For handling memory leaks, it's important to ensure that C++ objects are appropriately finalized. Using `Gc.finalise` can be useful but limited; explicit finalizers in C++ may be warranted depending on how these objects are managed in-memory. 
   - Consider implementing finalizers in C++ using smart pointers for better memory handling.
